<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">Hurricane Ike</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div class="noprint" id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>
<div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">
					Jump to:					<a href="#mw-head">navigation</a>, 					<a href="#p-search">search</a>
</div>

For other uses, see <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Ike" title="Tropical Storm Ike">Tropical Storm Ike</a>.</div>

<p><b>Hurricane Ike</b> (pronounced <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="/aɪ/: 'i' in 'tide'">aɪ</span><span title="'k' in 'kind'">k</span></span>/</a></span></span>) was a powerful <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone" title="Tropical cyclone">tropical cyclone</a> that swept through portions of the <a href="/wiki/Greater_Antilles" title="Greater Antilles">Greater Antilles</a> and <a href="/wiki/Northern_America" title="Northern America">Northern America</a> in September <a href="/wiki/2008_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2008 Atlantic hurricane season">2008</a>, wreaking havoc on infrastructure and agriculture, particularly in <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a> and <a href="/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">Texas</a>. Other locations were also seriously affected by Ike, which was ultimately the <a href="/wiki/List_of_costliest_Atlantic_hurricanes" title="List of costliest Atlantic hurricanes">third-costliest</a> of any <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_hurricane" title="Atlantic hurricane">Atlantic hurricane</a> and resulted in $37.5 billion in damages, with only hurricanes <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Sandy" title="Hurricane Sandy">Sandy</a> (2012) and <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Katrina" title="Hurricane Katrina">Katrina</a> (2005) estimated higher.</p>
<p>Ike developed from a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_wave" title="Tropical wave">tropical wave</a> west of <a href="/wiki/Cape_Verde" title="Cape Verde">Cape Verde</a> on September 1<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UTC_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-UTC-1">[nb 1]</a></sup> and strengthened to a peak intensity as a <a href="/wiki/List_of_Category_4_Atlantic_hurricanes" title="List of Category 4 Atlantic hurricanes">Category 4 hurricane</a> over the open waters of the central Atlantic on September 4 as it tracked westward. Several fluctuations in strength occurred before Ike made <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Landfall_(meteorology)" title="Landfall (meteorology)">landfall</a> on eastern Cuba on September 8. The hurricane weakened prior to continuing into the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Mexico" title="Gulf of Mexico">Gulf of Mexico</a>, but increased its intensity by the time of its final landfall on <a href="/wiki/Galveston,_Texas" title="Galveston, Texas">Galveston, Texas</a> on September 13. The remnants of Ike continued to track across the United States and into Canada, causing considerable damage inland, before dissipating two days later.</p>
<p>Ike was blamed for at least 195 deaths. Of these deaths, 74 were in <a href="/wiki/Haiti" title="Haiti">Haiti</a>, which was already trying to recover from the impact of three storms (<a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Fay_(2008)" title="Tropical Storm Fay (2008)">Fay</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Gustav" title="Hurricane Gustav">Gustav</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hurricane_Hanna_(2008)" title="Hurricane Hanna (2008)">Hanna</a>) which had made landfall that same year. Seven people were killed in Cuba by Ike.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USATodayCuba_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-USATodayCuba-2">[1]</a></sup> In the United States, 113 people were reported killed, directly or indirectly, and 16 were still missing as of August 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IkeTCR_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-IkeTCR-3">[2]</a></sup> Due to its immense size, Ike caused devastation from the <a href="/wiki/Louisiana" title="Louisiana">Louisiana</a> coastline all the way to the <a href="/wiki/Kenedy_County,_Texas" title="Kenedy County, Texas">Kenedy County</a> region near <a href="/wiki/Corpus_Christi,_Texas" title="Corpus Christi, Texas">Corpus Christi, Texas</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[3]</a></sup> In addition, Ike caused flooding and significant damage along the <a href="/wiki/Mississippi" title="Mississippi">Mississippi</a> coastline and the <a href="/wiki/Florida_Panhandle" title="Florida Panhandle">Florida Panhandle</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[4]</a></sup> Damages from Ike in U.S. coastal and inland areas are estimated at $29.5 billion (2008 USD),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IkeTCR_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-IkeTCR-3">[2]</a></sup> with additional damage of $7.3 billion in Cuba (the costliest storm ever in that country), $200 million in the Bahamas, and $500 million in the <a href="/wiki/Turks_and_Caicos_Islands" title="Turks and Caicos Islands">Turks and Caicos</a>, amounting to a total of at least $37.5 billion in damage. Ike is currently the <a href="/wiki/List_of_costliest_Atlantic_hurricanes" title="List of costliest Atlantic hurricanes">third-costliest Atlantic hurricane</a> of all time, only surpassed by <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Katrina" title="Hurricane Katrina">Hurricane Katrina</a> in 2005, and later by <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Sandy" title="Hurricane Sandy">Hurricane Sandy</a> in 2012,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[5]</a></sup> though initial cost estimates for Hurricanes <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Harvey" title="Hurricane Harvey">Harvey</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lee2_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lee2-7">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-190billion_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-190billion-8">[7]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Irma" title="Hurricane Irma">Irma</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Guardian_death_toll_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-The_Guardian_death_toll-10">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Harvey_and_Irma_economic_cost_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-Harvey_and_Irma_economic_cost-14">[13]</a></sup> indicate both will surpass Ike. The search-and-rescue operation after Ike is the largest search-and-rescue operation in Texas history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-largestrescue_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-largestrescue-15">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p>Ike was the third <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Major_hurricane" title="Major hurricane">major hurricane</a> of the <a href="/wiki/2008_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2008 Atlantic hurricane season">2008 Atlantic hurricane season</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IkeTCR_3-2"><a href="#cite_note-IkeTCR-3">[2]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Meteorological_history">Meteorological history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Ike&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Meteorological history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ike_2008_track.png"><img alt="Map showing the path of a tropical cyclone, which generally moves from right to left. The track crosses over several landmasses to the left of the image, before curving towards the upper half of the map." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="633" data-file-width="1024" height="136" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Ike_2008_track.png/220px-Ike_2008_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Ike_2008_track.png/330px-Ike_2008_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Ike_2008_track.png/440px-Ike_2008_track.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ike_2008_track.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Map plotting the track and intensity of the storm, according to the <a href="/wiki/Saffir%E2%80%93Simpson_scale" title="Saffir–Simpson scale">Saffir–Simpson scale</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The origins of Hurricane Ike can be traced back to a well-defined <a href="/wiki/Tropical_wave" title="Tropical wave">tropical wave</a> first identified by the <a href="/wiki/National_Hurricane_Center" title="National Hurricane Center">National Hurricane Center</a> <small>(NHC)</small> just within the western coast of Africa on August 28.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TCR1_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-TCR1-16">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TWO-800-0828_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-TWO-800-0828-17">[16]</a></sup> Despite the development of a <a href="/wiki/Low-pressure_area" title="Low-pressure area">low-pressure area</a> associated with the wave and signs of organization within favorable conditions near the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cape_Verde_Islands" title="Cape Verde Islands">Cape Verde Islands</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TWO-2000-0828_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-TWO-2000-0828-18">[17]</a></sup> the system was only able to generate intermittent <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Convection_(meteorology)" title="Convection (meteorology)">thunderstorm activity</a>. The broad low-pressure continued to track westward and was considered to have become sufficiently organized to be classified as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tropical_depression" title="Tropical depression">tropical depression</a> at 06:00 <a href="/wiki/Coordinated_Universal_Time" title="Coordinated Universal Time">UTC</a> on September 1. By this time the cyclone had tracked 780 miles (1,260 kilometers) west of Cape Verde. Although post-analysis indicated that the depression reached <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tropical_storm" title="Tropical storm">tropical storm</a> strength at 12:00 UTC that day,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TCR2_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-TCR2-19">[18]</a></sup> operationally the NHC began issuing advisories on Ike three hours later, by which time the system had already gained numerous curved <a href="/wiki/Rainband" title="Rainband">rainbands</a> and well-established <a href="/wiki/Outflow_(meteorology)" title="Outflow (meteorology)">outflow</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AdvDisc1_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-AdvDisc1-20">[19]</a></sup> Over the next few hours, Ike developed additional rainbands,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AdvDisc3_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-AdvDisc3-21">[20]</a></sup> but failed to a centralized area of convection due to the presence of dry air to the storm's south and its location in an area with only marginally favorable <a href="/wiki/Sea_surface_temperature" title="Sea surface temperature">sea surface temperatures</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AdvDisc4_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-AdvDisc4-22">[21]</a></sup> These factors were also responsible for Ike's slow developmental trend that began after formation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TCR2_19-1"><a href="#cite_note-TCR2-19">[18]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:234613W_sm.gif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="400" data-file-width="500" height="176" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/234613W_sm.gif/220px-234613W_sm.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/234613W_sm.gif/330px-234613W_sm.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/234613W_sm.gif/440px-234613W_sm.gif 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:234613W_sm.gif" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Meteorological prediction of Ike's path on September 3, 2008</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Ike's gradual strengthening began to quicken early on September 3, with the strengthening of an intense rainband around the center of the storm. At roughly 15:00 UTC that day, <a href="/wiki/Microwave_imaging" title="Microwave imaging">microwave imaging</a> indicated that a primordial <a href="/wiki/Eye_(cyclone)" title="Eye (cyclone)">eye</a> was developing within the intensifying tropical storm.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TCR2_19-2"><a href="#cite_note-TCR2-19">[18]</a></sup> Tracking northwestward, the NHC upgraded Ike to hurricane status at 18:00 UTC based on <a href="/wiki/Dvorak_technique" title="Dvorak technique">objective satellite intensity estimates</a> and the appearance of the eye on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Visible_light" title="Visible light">visible satellite imagery</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TCR2_19-3"><a href="#cite_note-TCR2-19">[18]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AdvDisc10_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-AdvDisc10-23">[22]</a></sup> During this time, Ike was centered 690 mi (1,110 km) east-northeast of the <a href="/wiki/Leeward_Islands" title="Leeward Islands">Leeward Islands</a> and was tracking west-northwestward as a result of a weakened <a href="/wiki/Subtropical_ridge" title="Subtropical ridge">subtropical ridge</a> to its northeast.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TCR2_19-4"><a href="#cite_note-TCR2-19">[18]</a></sup> Ike's placement in an area with virtually no <a href="/wiki/Wind_shear" title="Wind shear">wind shear</a> allowed for the hurricane to undergo <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Explosive_intensification" title="Explosive intensification">explosive intensification</a> despite unfavorable upper-level winds to its north,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AdvDisc10_23-1"><a href="#cite_note-AdvDisc10-23">[22]</a></sup> reaching <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Major_hurricane" title="Major hurricane">major hurricane</a> strength six hours after its designation as a hurricane.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AdvDisc11_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-AdvDisc11-24">[23]</a></sup> At 06:00 UTC on September 4, Ike peaked with <a href="/wiki/Maximum_sustained_wind" title="Maximum sustained wind">maximum sustained winds</a> of 145 miles per hour (233 kilometers per hour) and a minimum <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Barometric_pressure" title="Barometric pressure">barometric pressure</a> of 935 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">millibars</a> (27.6 <a href="/wiki/Inch_of_mercury" title="Inch of mercury">inches of mercury</a>), making the storm a <a href="/wiki/List_of_Category_4_Atlantic_hurricanes" title="List of Category 4 Atlantic hurricanes">Category 4</a> on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saffir%E2%80%93Simpson_hurricane_wind_scale" title="Saffir–Simpson hurricane wind scale">Saffir–Simpson hurricane wind scale</a>. After peaking in strength, a ridge of high pressure to the storm's west strengthened, causing Ike to track towards the southwest—a path unusual for the time of year. However, this track also brought the storm into an area of strong wind shear,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TCR2_19-5"><a href="#cite_note-TCR2-19">[18]</a></sup> causing the storm to become asymmetric in structure late on September 4 and weaken,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AdvDisc14_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-AdvDisc14-25">[24]</a></sup> briefly dropping below major hurricane status on September 6 while 150 miles (240 km) east of <a href="/wiki/Grand_Turk_Island" title="Grand Turk Island">Grand Turk Island</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Adv22_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-Adv22-26">[25]</a></sup> Although wind shear abated and allowed for reintensification, Ike would fluctuate in strength over the next few days. After passing near the <a href="/wiki/Turks_and_Caicos_Islands" title="Turks and Caicos Islands">Turks and Caicos Islands</a>, Ike made its first <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Landfall_(meteorology)" title="Landfall (meteorology)">landfall</a> on <a href="/wiki/Inagua" title="Inagua">Inagua</a> in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bahamas" title="Bahamas">Bahamas</a> at 13:00 UTC on September 7 with winds of 125 mph (201 km/h).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TCR3_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-TCR3-27">[26]</a></sup></p>
<p>After passing over Inagua,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TCR3_27-1"><a href="#cite_note-TCR3-27">[26]</a></sup> the development of a double eyewall—a feature that usually denotes the beginning of an <a href="/wiki/Eyewall_replacement_cycle" title="Eyewall replacement cycle">eyewall replacement cycle</a>—slightly weakened Ike late on September 7.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Adv27_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-Adv27-28">[27]</a></sup> However, the hurricane was able to reintensify and reach Category 4 intensity for a final time before making landfall near Cabo Lucrecia on the coast of <a href="/wiki/Holgu%C3%ADn_Province" title="Holguín Province">Holguín Province</a> in <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a> by 00:00 UTC the next day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TCR3_27-2"><a href="#cite_note-TCR3-27">[26]</a></sup> Although Ike remained well-defined for most of its crossing of eastern Cuba,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Adv30_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-Adv30-29">[28]</a></sup> the hurricane's core had become disrupted by the time it had reached the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Sea" title="Caribbean Sea">Caribbean Sea</a> after spending a few hours over land.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Adv31_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-Adv31-30">[29]</a></sup> Over the next day, Ike tracked westward, paralleling the southern coast of Cuba without much intensification; at times the center of the hurricane was within 12 mi (19 km) of the island. At around 14:00 UTC on September 9, Ike made a second Cuban landfall, this time on Punta La Capitana in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pinar_del_Rio" title="Pinar del Rio">Pinar del Rio</a>, with winds of 80 mph (130 km/h). Roughly six hours later, the hurricane emerged into the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Mexico" title="Gulf of Mexico">Gulf of Mexico</a> as a slightly weakened system.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TCR3_27-3"><a href="#cite_note-TCR3-27">[26]</a></sup></p>
<p>Despite tracking back over water, Ike's prolonged interaction with Cuba had greatly disrupted the system's core, and instead of quickly strengthening and coalescing, the storm's wind field instead grew and only gradual intensification ensued.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TCR3_27-4"><a href="#cite_note-TCR3-27">[26]</a></sup> Due to the storm's comparatively small inner core and intensity of the outer rainbands,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Adv40_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-Adv40-31">[30]</a></sup> an eyewall replacement cycle took place, preventing Ike from rapidly intensifying. At around the same time, a <a href="/wiki/High-pressure_area" title="High-pressure area">high-pressure area</a> strengthened to the hurricane's north, steering the cyclone further west than initially anticipated. Moving over the warm waters of the <a href="/wiki/Loop_Current" title="Loop Current">Loop Current</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TCR3_27-5"><a href="#cite_note-TCR3-27">[26]</a></sup> Ike reached a secondary minimum in barometric pressure on 00:00 UTC with an estimate of 944 mbar (27.9 inHg); though winds would continue to strengthen afterward, the storm's pressure would rise.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TCR16_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-TCR16-32">[31]</a></sup> By late on September 12, Ike had reached the western edge of the nearby <a href="/wiki/High-pressure_area" title="High-pressure area">high-pressure area</a> and began to curve northward. The formation of an eye just prior to landfall resulted in a slight increase in winds,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TCR3_27-6"><a href="#cite_note-TCR3-27">[26]</a></sup> and at 0700 UTC on September 13, Ike made landfall on the northeast end of <a href="/wiki/Galveston_Island" title="Galveston Island">Galveston Island</a> in <a href="/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">Texas</a>, with a minimum barometric pressure of 950 mbar (28 inHg) and sustained winds of 110 mph (180 km/h), making Ike a Category 2 hurricane.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TCR16_32-1"><a href="#cite_note-TCR16-32">[31]</a></sup> After tracking inland, Ike weakened as it sped northward and later northeastward, weakening to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tropical_storm" title="Tropical storm">tropical storm</a> status east of <a href="/wiki/Palestine,_Texas" title="Palestine, Texas">Palestine, Texas</a> late on September 13 and later becoming a powerful <a href="/wiki/Extratropical_cyclone" title="Extratropical cyclone">extratropical cyclone</a> on September 14 over the <a href="/wiki/Ozarks" title="Ozarks">Ozarks</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TCR3_27-7"><a href="#cite_note-TCR3-27">[26]</a></sup> A more steady weakening phase ensued, and after tracking across southern <a href="/wiki/Ontario" title="Ontario">Ontario</a> and <a href="/wiki/Quebec" title="Quebec">Quebec</a>, the remnants of Ike were absorbed by another extratropical low near the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Lawrence_River" title="St. Lawrence River">St. Lawrence River</a>, on September 15.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TCR4_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-TCR4-33">[32]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Preparations">Preparations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Ike&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Preparations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Turks_and_Caicos_and_the_Bahamas">Turks and Caicos and the Bahamas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Ike&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Turks and Caicos and the Bahamas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Fearing a repeat of <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Donna" title="Hurricane Donna">Hurricane Donna</a> in <a href="/wiki/1960_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="1960 Atlantic hurricane season">1960</a>, the overseas branch of the <a href="/wiki/British_Red_Cross" title="British Red Cross">British Red Cross</a> began preparing contingency plans for 2,000 families considered to be at risk from Ike. A group of 260 Chinese construction workers stuck on <a href="/wiki/Middle_Caicos" title="Middle Caicos">Middle Caicos</a> after the passage of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hurricane_Hanna_(2008)" title="Hurricane Hanna (2008)">Hurricane Hanna</a> were evacuated by the British Red Cross.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RedCrossRespTC_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-RedCrossRespTC-34">[33]</a></sup> Immediately before the storm struck, 348 people on Grand Turk were put into emergency shelters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TCAppealHealthEmergency_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-TCAppealHealthEmergency-35">[34]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Florida">Florida</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Ike&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Florida">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:USArmyHurricaneIke.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3872" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/USArmyHurricaneIke.jpg/220px-USArmyHurricaneIke.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/USArmyHurricaneIke.jpg/330px-USArmyHurricaneIke.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/USArmyHurricaneIke.jpg/440px-USArmyHurricaneIke.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:USArmyHurricaneIke.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A <a href="/wiki/Florida_Army_National_Guard" title="Florida Army National Guard">Florida Army National Guardsman</a> uses a Single Mobile User Case Set to send a situation report on ongoing preparations for Hurricane Ike in <a href="/wiki/Key_West,_Florida" title="Key West, Florida">Key West, Florida</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On September 5, Florida Governor <a href="/wiki/Charlie_Crist" title="Charlie Crist">Charlie Crist</a> declared a state of emergency in advance of Ike's arrival, (which was expected to be as early as September 8). Authorities in <a href="/wiki/Key_West" title="Key West">Key West</a> issued a mandatory evacuation for all visitors for September 6. The <a href="/wiki/Federal_Emergency_Management_Agency" title="Federal Emergency Management Agency">Federal Emergency Management Agency</a> (FEMA) positioned supplies, and emergency response crews in Florida and along the Gulf Coast.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Florida_Keys" title="Florida Keys">Florida Keys</a> officials began evacuations on the low-lying chain of islands in phases, starting at the end in <a href="/wiki/Key_West" title="Key West">Key West</a> by 8 am Sunday and continuing throughout the day—at noon for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Middle_Keys" title="Middle Keys">Middle Keys</a>, and at 4 pm for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Upper_Keys" title="Upper Keys">Upper Keys</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Key_Largo" title="Key Largo">Key Largo</a>. Visitors were told to leave on Saturday.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[35]</a></sup> Overall 15,000 tourists evacuated, but the storm stayed to the south, only causing minor beach erosion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IkeTCR_3-3"><a href="#cite_note-IkeTCR-3">[2]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Texas">Texas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Ike&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Texas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:After_Hurricane_Ike_in_Texas.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1996" data-file-width="3000" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/After_Hurricane_Ike_in_Texas.jpg/220px-After_Hurricane_Ike_in_Texas.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/After_Hurricane_Ike_in_Texas.jpg/330px-After_Hurricane_Ike_in_Texas.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/After_Hurricane_Ike_in_Texas.jpg/440px-After_Hurricane_Ike_in_Texas.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:After_Hurricane_Ike_in_Texas.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A US-Air Force Staff Sergeant receives a hug from a resident after Hurricane Ike, September 13, 2008.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On September 7, The Texas Water/Wastewater Agency Response Network (TXWARN)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[36]</a></sup> activated its 700-member utility mutual aid network and began coordination with the State Emergency Operations Center and the Texas Commission on Environmental Quality (TCEQ) to begin preparations and notifications to utilities to prepare for Ike.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[37]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rural_Water" title="Rural Water">State rural water associations</a> activated mutual aid networks to prepare for the landfall of Ike while still providing assistance to areas affected by <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Gustav" title="Hurricane Gustav">Hurricane Gustav</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[38]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[39]</a></sup> The Texas Rural Water Association held meetings with state agencies on September 9, to plan for landfall along the Texas Gulf Coast.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[40]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[41]</a></sup></p>
<p>On September 11, forecasting models began to show Ike making landfall just south of Galveston. City Manager Steven LeBlanc late Wednesday issued a mandatory evacuation order for the low-lying west end of <a href="/wiki/Galveston_Island" title="Galveston Island">Galveston Island</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[42]</a></sup> Later, the mandatory evacuation order was extended to the entire island of Galveston, as well as low-lying areas around <a href="/wiki/Houston" title="Houston">Houston</a>, Texas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[43]</a></sup> Mandatory evacuations were also ordered for <a href="/wiki/Jefferson_County,_Texas" title="Jefferson County, Texas">Jefferson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Orange_County,_Texas" title="Orange County, Texas">Orange</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Chambers_County,_Texas" title="Chambers County, Texas">Chambers</a> counties located east of Houston. Voluntary evacuations were in effect for <a href="/wiki/Hardin_County,_Texas" title="Hardin County, Texas">Hardin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tyler_County,_Texas" title="Tyler County, Texas">Tyler</a> as well as <a href="/wiki/Newton_County,_Texas" title="Newton County, Texas">Newton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jasper_County,_Texas" title="Jasper County, Texas">Jasper</a> counties.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[44]</a></sup> Residents evacuating ahead of Ike were received by emergency workers in the Dallas/Fort Worth(DFW) Metroplex where they were provided a place of refuge, medical treatment, and provisions. In addition to the orders of local and state officials, federal officials were thoroughly involved in evacuation decisions. On September 10, U.S. President <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a> made an emergency declaration for Texas, making more federal help available for preparations and evacuations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[45]</a></sup> More than one million people evacuated in advance of Hurricane Ike, but more than 100,000 people did not.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CutterSmith2009_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-CutterSmith2009-47">[46]</a></sup></p>
<p>At 8:19 pm (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Central_Daylight_Time_(North_America)" title="Central Daylight Time (North America)">CDT</a>) September 11, the <a href="/wiki/National_Weather_Service" title="National Weather Service">National Weather Service</a> in <a href="/wiki/Houston" title="Houston">Houston</a>/<a href="/wiki/Galveston,_Texas" title="Galveston, Texas">Galveston, Texas</a> issued a strongly worded bulletin, regarding storm surge along the shoreline of <a href="/wiki/Galveston_Bay" title="Galveston Bay">Galveston Bay</a>. The bulletin advised that residents living in single-family homes in some parts of coastal Texas faced "certain death" if they did not heed orders to evacuate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[47]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-49">[48]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNNDeath1_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-CNNDeath1-50">[49]</a></sup> Reports said as many as 40 percent of Galveston's citizens did not pay attention to the warnings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[50]</a></sup> It was feared to be much the same in Port Arthur, and it was predicted that low-lying areas between <a href="/wiki/Morgan_City,_Louisiana" title="Morgan City, Louisiana">Morgan City, Louisiana</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baffin_Bay,_Texas" title="Baffin Bay, Texas">Baffin Bay, Texas</a>, particularly those areas east of Ike's projected eye landfall would experience the greatest damage from storm surges of up to 20 feet (6.1 m).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[51]</a></sup></p>
<p>The price of gas increased in the expectation of damage to some of the numerous oil refineries along the South Texas coast, or at least delays in production from the oil and gas platforms in the Gulf of Mexico.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[52]</a></sup> 14 oil refineries shut down production and nearly 150 oil tankers and cargo ships waited off-shore as every port from <a href="/wiki/Lake_Charles,_Louisiana" title="Lake Charles, Louisiana">Lake Charles, Louisiana</a> to <a href="/wiki/Corpus_Christi,_Texas" title="Corpus Christi, Texas">Corpus Christi, Texas</a> shut down in preparation for the storm.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IkeTCR_3-4"><a href="#cite_note-IkeTCR-3">[2]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Impact">Impact</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Ike&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Impact">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Turks_and_Caicos_Islands_and_The_Bahamas">Turks and Caicos Islands and The Bahamas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Ike&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Turks and Caicos Islands and The Bahamas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Caribbean_winter_2008_2009_2_969.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Caribbean_winter_2008_2009_2_969.JPG/220px-Caribbean_winter_2008_2009_2_969.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Caribbean_winter_2008_2009_2_969.JPG/330px-Caribbean_winter_2008_2009_2_969.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Caribbean_winter_2008_2009_2_969.JPG/440px-Caribbean_winter_2008_2009_2_969.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Caribbean_winter_2008_2009_2_969.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Numerous hurricane-damaged houses, buildings, and structures were still to be found in early January 2009 on <a href="/wiki/Grand_Turk_Island" title="Grand Turk Island">Grand Turk</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Turks_.26_Caicos_Weekly_News_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-Turks_.26_Caicos_Weekly_News-54">[53]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Power was lost throughout <a href="/wiki/Grand_Turk_Island" title="Grand Turk Island">Grand Turk Island</a>, an estimated 80%–95% of the houses there were damaged, 20% of which were a total loss.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IkeTCR_3-6"><a href="#cite_note-IkeTCR-3">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TCAppealHealthEmergency_35-1"><a href="#cite_note-TCAppealHealthEmergency-35">[34]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IkeUSAtoday_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-IkeUSAtoday-55">[54]</a></sup> There was also significant structural damage to roofs and buildings containing health services resulting in the disruption of most health services.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TCAppealHealthEmergency_35-2"><a href="#cite_note-TCAppealHealthEmergency-35">[34]</a></sup> The local pharmacy roof collapsed, destroying the area's prescription drug supply, the police station, and the prison was significantly damaged and local supplies facilities were either damaged or destroyed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TCAppealHealthEmergency_35-3"><a href="#cite_note-TCAppealHealthEmergency-35">[34]</a></sup> Water and electricity were also disrupted but since have been restored.</p>
<p>Meanwhile, in South Caicos, 95% of the houses were also damaged, with over one-third significantly damaged or destroyed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IkeTCR_3-7"><a href="#cite_note-IkeTCR-3">[2]</a></sup> A two-year-old cruise ship terminal in South Caicos owned by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Carnival_Cruise_Lines" title="Carnival Cruise Lines">Carnival Cruise Lines</a> was significantly damaged.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IkeTCR_3-8"><a href="#cite_note-IkeTCR-3">[2]</a></sup> Damage also occurred on other islands, mostly agricultural or the fishing industry, but in general, the damage was minor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IkeTCR_3-9"><a href="#cite_note-IkeTCR-3">[2]</a></sup></p>
<p>Buildings on the islands have been severely weakened and 750 people have lost their homes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-British_Red_Cross_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-British_Red_Cross-56">[55]</a></sup> Due to the extent and magnitude of damage and affected population, the <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_the_Turks_and_Caicos_Islands" title="Politics of the Turks and Caicos Islands">Government of the Turks and Caicos</a> declared Grand Turk and South Caicos Islands disaster areas.</p>
<p>In <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Great_Inagua_Island" title="Great Inagua Island">Great Inagua Island</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Bahamas" title="The Bahamas">The Bahamas</a>, eighty percent of houses sustained damage with almost a third of them having significant damage. The local <a href="/wiki/Morton_Salt" title="Morton Salt">Morton Salt</a> factory was damaged and shut down operations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IkeTCR_3-10"><a href="#cite_note-IkeTCR-3">[2]</a></sup> A few outlining islands suffered minor damage and no casualties was reported. Overall damage from the Turks and Caicos and The Bahamas was estimated between $50 million and $200 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IkeTCR_3-11"><a href="#cite_note-IkeTCR-3">[2]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Haiti">Haiti</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Ike&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Haiti">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Destroyed_school_in_Port-Au-Prince.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1528" data-file-width="2300" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Destroyed_school_in_Port-Au-Prince.jpg/220px-Destroyed_school_in_Port-Au-Prince.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Destroyed_school_in_Port-Au-Prince.jpg/330px-Destroyed_school_in_Port-Au-Prince.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Destroyed_school_in_Port-Au-Prince.jpg/440px-Destroyed_school_in_Port-Au-Prince.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Destroyed_school_in_Port-Au-Prince.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The remains of a school in Port-au-Prince, Haiti on September 15, 2008</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The outer bands of Ike caused additional flooding in <a href="/wiki/Haiti" title="Haiti">Haiti</a>, which was already devastated by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hurricane_Hanna_(2008)" title="Hurricane Hanna (2008)">Hanna</a> and also hit hard by <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Fay_(2008)" title="Tropical Storm Fay (2008)">Fay</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Gustav" title="Hurricane Gustav">Gustav</a>. The last bridge still standing into the city of <a href="/wiki/Gona%C3%AFves" title="Gonaïves">Gonaïves</a> was washed away, slowing relief in the community considerably and creating a deep humanitarian and food crisis in the hard-hit region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IkeTCR_3-12"><a href="#cite_note-IkeTCR-3">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Guardianhaiti_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-Guardianhaiti-57">[56]</a></sup> 74 deaths were reported in Haiti from Ike, most of which were in the coastal community of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cabaret,_Haiti" title="Cabaret, Haiti">Cabaret</a> which was swept away by floodwaters and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mudslide" title="Mudslide">mudslides</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IkeTCR_3-13"><a href="#cite_note-IkeTCR-3">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DetNews_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-DetNews-58">[57]</a></sup> Haitian Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Mich%C3%A8le_Pierre-Louis" title="Michèle Pierre-Louis">Michèle Pierre-Louis</a> called for help at the end of the week, saying that four storms in three weeks have left over 550 dead and as many as one million homeless.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC7613851_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-BBC7613851-59">[58]</a></sup> She also said that parts of Gonaïves were so severely damaged that the city may have to be rebuilt elsewhere.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC7613851_59-1"><a href="#cite_note-BBC7613851-59">[58]</a></sup> Two additional deaths were reported in the <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic" title="Dominican Republic">Dominican Republic</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IkeTCR_3-14"><a href="#cite_note-IkeTCR-3">[2]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuba">Cuba</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Ike&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Cuba">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Ivan" title="Hurricane Ivan">Ivan</a></th>
<td><a href="/wiki/2004_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2004 Atlantic hurricane season">2004</a></td>
<td><span class="sortkey" style="display:none">7009120000000000000♠</span>$1.2 billion</td>
<td><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WMO_2004_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-WMO_2004-66">[65]</a></sup></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Charley" title="Hurricane Charley">Charley</a></th>
<td><a href="/wiki/2004_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2004 Atlantic hurricane season">2004</a></td>
<td><span class="sortkey" style="display:none">7008923000000000000♠</span>$923 million</td>
<td><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WMO_2004_66-1"><a href="#cite_note-WMO_2004-66">[65]</a></sup></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>About 2.6 million Cubans, a fourth of the population, were evacuated ahead of Ike.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nbccuba_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-nbccuba-67">[66]</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Baracoa" title="Baracoa">Baracoa</a>, 200 homes were reported to be destroyed and waves were running 23 ft (7 m) high and peaked at 40 ft (12 m) in different areas of Cuba. The Category 4 hurricane made landfall on September 8 on the north coast of eastern Cuba in the province of <a href="/wiki/Holgu%C3%ADn" title="Holguín">Holguín</a> near Puerto de Sama, with sustained winds of about 130 mph (209 km/h),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IkeTCR_3-15"><a href="#cite_note-IkeTCR-3">[2]</a></sup> causing widespread flooding and damage to the eastern provinces.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IkeTCR_3-16"><a href="#cite_note-IkeTCR-3">[2]</a></sup> It passed across the central provinces of Holguín, Las Tunas, and Camagüey, emerging over the sea to the south of Cuba during the day. Ike dropped to Category One intensity by the time it crossed the island.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[67]</a></sup> It then followed the southern coast of Cuba and crossed the western end of the island in <a href="/wiki/Pinar_del_R%C3%ADo_Province" title="Pinar del Río Province">Pinar del Río Province</a>, close to the path taken by <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Gustav" title="Hurricane Gustav">Hurricane Gustav</a> ten days previously. The western areas of Cuba, already devastated by just 10 days before Ike hit, suffered additional major flooding from the rain and storm surge.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USATodayCuba_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-USATodayCuba-2">[1]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sugar_cane" title="Sugar cane">sugar cane</a> crop was devastated, with over 3,400 square kilometres (1,300 sq mi) destroyed. The <a href="/wiki/Banana" title="Banana">banana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yucca" title="Yucca">yucca</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coffee" title="Coffee">coffee</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Corn" title="Corn">corn</a> crop also suffered significant damage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IkeTCR_3-17"><a href="#cite_note-IkeTCR-3">[2]</a></sup> Alongside Gustav, they were described as the "worst ever" storms by Cuban officials.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBCCuba_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-BBCCuba-69">[68]</a></sup></p>
<p>In total, seven people were killed in Cuba from Ike due to drowning or collapsing structures.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USATodayCuba_2-2"><a href="#cite_note-USATodayCuba-2">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IkeTCR_3-18"><a href="#cite_note-IkeTCR-3">[2]</a></sup> Over 300,000 houses were damaged, with an estimated 43,000 a total loss.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IkeTCR_3-19"><a href="#cite_note-IkeTCR-3">[2]</a></sup> The combined damage estimate from Ike and Gustav, and succeeding Paloma is about $9.7 billion (USD), with $7.3 billion of that from Ike, making Ike the most destructive hurricane in Cuban history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WMOCuba_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-WMOCuba-70">[69]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_States">United States</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Ike&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: United States">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_Ike_NEXRAD_radar_animation.gif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="761" data-file-width="1370" height="122" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Hurricane_Ike_NEXRAD_radar_animation.gif/220px-Hurricane_Ike_NEXRAD_radar_animation.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Hurricane_Ike_NEXRAD_radar_animation.gif/330px-Hurricane_Ike_NEXRAD_radar_animation.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Hurricane_Ike_NEXRAD_radar_animation.gif/440px-Hurricane_Ike_NEXRAD_radar_animation.gif 2x" width="220"/></a>

</div>
</div>
