<tr class="small">
<th colspan="6">Source: National Hurricane Center<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dead_2011_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-Dead_2011-71">[70]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[71]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[72]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[nb 2]</a></sup></th>
</tr>
</table>
<p>Due to the intensity of the storm, Texas closed many of its chemical plants and oil refineries. Because much of the United States oil refining capacity is located in Texas, the closings caused a temporary increase in the prices of gasoline, home heating oil, and natural gas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[73]</a></sup> Increases were particularly high in <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina" title="North Carolina">North Carolina</a>, especially in the mountains, where average prices were as much as 60 cents higher than the national average.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[74]</a></sup> The closing of refineries so soon after Hurricane Gustav, and the time required to restart production, also resulted in shortages of gasoline in such places as the Carolinas and Tennessee, partly as a result of <a href="/wiki/Panic_buying" title="Panic buying">panic buying</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[75]</a></sup> 113 direct and indirect deaths have been reported in the US, including 85 in Texas (18 direct), eight in <a href="/wiki/Louisiana" title="Louisiana">Louisiana</a>, one in <a href="/wiki/Arkansas" title="Arkansas">Arkansas</a>, two in <a href="/wiki/Tennessee" title="Tennessee">Tennessee</a>, one in <a href="/wiki/Kentucky" title="Kentucky">Kentucky</a>, seven in <a href="/wiki/Indiana" title="Indiana">Indiana</a>, four in <a href="/wiki/Missouri" title="Missouri">Missouri</a>, two in <a href="/wiki/Illinois" title="Illinois">Illinois</a>, two in <a href="/wiki/Michigan" title="Michigan">Michigan</a>, seven in <a href="/wiki/Ohio" title="Ohio">Ohio</a> and one in <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania" title="Pennsylvania">Pennsylvania</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IkeTCR_3-20"><a href="#cite_note-IkeTCR-3">[2]</a></sup> As of August 2011, 16 people remain unaccounted for, 11 of them in the Galveston area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IkeTCR_3-21"><a href="#cite_note-IkeTCR-3">[2]</a></sup> On September 15, 2008, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Congress" title="United States Congress">United States Congress</a> held a moment of silence for those who died in the hurricane.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="MV_Antalina">MV <i>Antalina</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Ike&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: MV Antalina">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>On September 11, the MV <i>Antalina</i>, a 584-foot (178 m) cargo ship, was among the ships that left <a href="/wiki/Port_Arthur,_Texas" title="Port Arthur, Texas">Port Arthur</a> to avoid the hurricane. The ship had a crew of 22 and carried a cargo of <a href="/wiki/Petroleum_coke" title="Petroleum coke">petroleum coke</a>. On September 12, the ship's engine failed, and the ship was adrift 90 nautical miles (170 km) from the shore. The crew unsuccessfully attempted to repair the engine and requested to be evacuated by the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Coast_Guard" title="United States Coast Guard">Coast Guard</a>, but the rescue mission was aborted because weather conditions were not within the safety parameters. The crew was forced to ride out the storm but kept in contact with the Coast Guard.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[76]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[77]</a></sup> The ship successfully rode out the storm and all 22 crew members were uninjured. On September 13, a tugboat was dispatched to return the vessel to port.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[78]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Louisiana">Louisiana</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Ike&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Louisiana">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_Ike_New_Iberia.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1500" data-file-width="2000" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Hurricane_Ike_New_Iberia.jpg/220px-Hurricane_Ike_New_Iberia.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Hurricane_Ike_New_Iberia.jpg/330px-Hurricane_Ike_New_Iberia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Hurricane_Ike_New_Iberia.jpg/440px-Hurricane_Ike_New_Iberia.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_Ike_New_Iberia.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A <a href="/wiki/United_States_Coast_Guard" title="United States Coast Guard">Coast Guard</a> helicopter flying over <a href="/wiki/New_Iberia,_Louisiana" title="New Iberia, Louisiana">New Iberia, Louisiana</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The storm surge ahead of Ike blew onshore of <a href="/wiki/Louisiana" title="Louisiana">Louisiana</a> well ahead of Ike's predicted landfall in Texas on September 13. Areas in coastal south-central and southwestern Louisiana, some of which were flooded by Gustav, were re-flooded as a result of Ike.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KATC_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-KATC-81">[79]</a></sup> Some areas that had not yet recovered from Gustav power outages received additional outages,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Time-Picayune_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-Time-Picayune-82">[80]</a></sup> of 200,000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EpochTimes_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-EpochTimes-83">[81]</a></sup> The hardest-hit areas were in and around <a href="/wiki/Cameron_Parish,_Louisiana" title="Cameron Parish, Louisiana">Cameron Parish</a>, with nearly every square inch of the coastline in that area was flooded heavily, reaching as far north as <a href="/wiki/Lake_Charles,_Louisiana" title="Lake Charles, Louisiana">Lake Charles</a>, nearly 30 miles inland.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IkeTCR_3-22"><a href="#cite_note-IkeTCR-3">[2]</a></sup> Hundreds of people had to be rescued,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KALB_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-KALB-84">[82]</a></sup> including 363 people who were rescued by Louisiana Department of Wildlife and Fisheries Search and Rescue teams in conjunction with the Louisiana National Guard and the U.S. Coast Guard.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[83]</a></sup></p>
<p>One person was killed in a flooded bayou in <a href="/wiki/Terrebonne_Parish,_Louisiana" title="Terrebonne Parish, Louisiana">Terrebonne Parish</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KPLC_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-KPLC-86">[84]</a></sup> and a wind-related death was reported near <a href="/wiki/Houma,_Louisiana" title="Houma, Louisiana">Houma</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KATC0915_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-KATC0915-87">[85]</a></sup> Two other deaths took place in a car crash in the evacuation phase in <a href="/wiki/Iberville_Parish,_Louisiana" title="Iberville Parish, Louisiana">Iberville Parish</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KATC2dead_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-KATC2dead-88">[86]</a></sup> and two other storm-related deaths in <a href="/wiki/Jefferson_Davis_Parish,_Louisiana" title="Jefferson Davis Parish, Louisiana">Jefferson Davis Parish</a> were caused by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Natural_causes" title="Natural causes">natural causes</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KATC0915_87-1"><a href="#cite_note-KATC0915-87">[85]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Texas_2">Texas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Ike&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Texas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Effects_of_Hurricane_Ike_in_Texas" title="Effects of Hurricane Ike in Texas">Effects of Hurricane Ike in Texas</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_Ike_Gilchrist_damage_edit.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1842" data-file-width="2511" height="161" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Hurricane_Ike_Gilchrist_damage_edit.jpg/220px-Hurricane_Ike_Gilchrist_damage_edit.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Hurricane_Ike_Gilchrist_damage_edit.jpg/330px-Hurricane_Ike_Gilchrist_damage_edit.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Hurricane_Ike_Gilchrist_damage_edit.jpg/440px-Hurricane_Ike_Gilchrist_damage_edit.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_Ike_Gilchrist_damage_edit.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Damage from Ike in <a href="/wiki/Gilchrist,_Texas" title="Gilchrist, Texas">Gilchrist</a>, which was largely destroyed by the hurricane</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On the morning of September 13, 2008, the eye of Hurricane Ike approached the upper Texas coast, making landfall at 2:10 am CDT over the east end of <a href="/wiki/Galveston_Island" title="Galveston Island">Galveston Island</a>, with a high storm surge, and travelled north up <a href="/wiki/Galveston_Bay" title="Galveston Bay">Galveston Bay</a>, along the east side of Houston <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IBlast_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-IBlast-89">[87]</a></sup> (<i>see <a href="/wiki/File:Ike2008filledrainblk.gif" title="File:Ike2008filledrainblk.gif">storm-path image</a></i>). People in low-lying areas who had not heeded evacuation orders, in single-family one- or two-story homes, were warned by the weather service that they faced "certain death" from the overnight storm surge.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNNDeath1_50-1"><a href="#cite_note-CNNDeath1-50">[49]</a></sup> Nearly 16,000 families in the Galveston-Houston area stayed in temporary shelters under federal housing programs, while 1700 were referred for assistance but could not be reached or were refused aid.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>In regional Texas towns, electrical power began failing on September 12 before 8 pm CDT,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNNDeath1_50-2"><a href="#cite_note-CNNDeath1-50">[49]</a></sup> leaving millions without power (estimates range from 2.8 million<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DOE_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-DOE-90">[88]</a></sup> to 4.5 million<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bloombergpower_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bloombergpower-91">[89]</a></sup> customers). Grocery store shelves in the Houston area were empty for weeks in the aftermath of the storm.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[90]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_Ike-38263.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2832" data-file-width="4256" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Hurricane_Ike-38263.jpg/220px-Hurricane_Ike-38263.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Hurricane_Ike-38263.jpg/330px-Hurricane_Ike-38263.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Hurricane_Ike-38263.jpg/440px-Hurricane_Ike-38263.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_Ike-38263.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Flood waters begin to rise in a neighborhood of <a href="/wiki/Bayou_Vista,_Texas" title="Bayou Vista, Texas">Bayou Vista, Texas</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Galveston,_Texas" title="Galveston, Texas">Galveston</a>, by 4 pm CDT (2100 UTC) on September 12, the rising storm surge began overtopping the 17-ft (5.2 m) <a href="/wiki/Galveston_Seawall" title="Galveston Seawall">Galveston Seawall</a>, which faces the Gulf of Mexico;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNNDeath1_50-3"><a href="#cite_note-CNNDeath1-50">[49]</a></sup> waves had been crashing along the seawall earlier, from 9 am CDT.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USA25_93-0"><a href="#cite_note-USA25-93">[91]</a></sup> Although Seawall Boulevard is elevated above the shoreline, many areas of town slope down behind the seawall to the lower elevation of <a href="/wiki/Galveston_Island" title="Galveston Island">Galveston Island</a>.</p>
<p>Even though there were advance evacuation plans, Mary Jo Naschke, spokesperson for the city of Galveston, estimated that (as of Friday morning) a quarter of the city's residents paid no attention to calls for them to evacuate, despite predictions that most of Galveston Island would suffer heavy flooding <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Storm_tide" title="Storm tide">storm tide</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USA25_93-1"><a href="#cite_note-USA25-93">[91]</a></sup> By 6 pm Friday night estimates varied as to how many of the 58,000 residents remained, but the figures of remaining residents were in the thousands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WSJcas_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-WSJcas-94">[92]</a></sup> Widespread flooding included downtown Galveston:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IBlast_89-1"><a href="#cite_note-IBlast-89">[87]</a></sup> six feet (2 m) deep inside the Galveston County Courthouse, and the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Texas_Medical_Branch" title="University of Texas Medical Branch">University of Texas Medical Branch</a>, the primary hospital in Galveston county, was dealt significant damage due to flooding. The wide-scale flooding caused failures to all the facilities systems and allowed mold to invade all the buildings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-texasmedicine_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-texasmedicine-95">[93]</a></sup> Tourist attractions on the island suffered various degrees of damage. The <a href="/wiki/Lone_Star_Flight_Museum" title="Lone Star Flight Museum">Lone Star Flight Museum</a> suffered massive damage, as the storm surge washed through the airport and hangars with about 8 feet (2.4 m) of water; however, <a href="/wiki/Moody_Gardens" title="Moody Gardens">Moody Gardens</a> was built with storms in mind and was able to withstand the worst of the storm.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[94]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_Ike-38265.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2056" data-file-width="4224" height="107" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Hurricane_Ike-38265.jpg/220px-Hurricane_Ike-38265.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Hurricane_Ike-38265.jpg/330px-Hurricane_Ike-38265.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Hurricane_Ike-38265.jpg/440px-Hurricane_Ike-38265.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_Ike-38265.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Flooding in Galveston, Texas</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In Houston, windows also broke in downtown buildings, including the 75-story <a href="/wiki/JPMorgan_Chase_Tower_(Houston)" title="JPMorgan Chase Tower (Houston)">JP Morgan Chase Tower</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IBlast_89-2"><a href="#cite_note-IBlast-89">[87]</a></sup> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Reliant_Stadium" title="Reliant Stadium">Reliant Stadium</a> lost part of its roof.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IkeTCR_3-23"><a href="#cite_note-IkeTCR-3">[2]</a></sup> As a result of the high wind and eye wall that passed directly through the city, power outages were a major problem. Some residents were without electricity for over a month. Because the storm system moved rapidly and did not linger over Houston, flooding was not a major problem for most of the city, as it normally is in a storm event, as a result of the relatively flat topography.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IBlast_89-3"><a href="#cite_note-IBlast-89">[87]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Houston_Morgan_Chase_Building_Ike.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3872" data-file-width="2592" height="329" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Houston_Morgan_Chase_Building_Ike.jpg/220px-Houston_Morgan_Chase_Building_Ike.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Houston_Morgan_Chase_Building_Ike.jpg/330px-Houston_Morgan_Chase_Building_Ike.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Houston_Morgan_Chase_Building_Ike.jpg/440px-Houston_Morgan_Chase_Building_Ike.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Houston_Morgan_Chase_Building_Ike.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Windows were broken throughout the <a href="/wiki/JPMorgan_Chase_Tower_(Houston)" title="JPMorgan Chase Tower (Houston)">JPMorgan Chase Tower</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On <a href="/wiki/Bolivar_Peninsula,_Texas" title="Bolivar Peninsula, Texas">Bolivar Peninsula, Texas</a>, dozens of people were rescued as flood waters exceeded 12 feet (3.7 m) above sea level in advance of the hurricane. Many residents, some trapped by high water on the road at Rollover Pass and others elsewhere along Bolivar Peninsula were not rescued. The peninsula bore the brunt of Ike's right-front quadrant, historically the worst part of a hurricane, and experienced catastrophic damage with the worst being between <a href="/wiki/Rollover_Pass" title="Rollover Pass">Rollover Pass</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gilchrist,_Texas" title="Gilchrist, Texas">Gilchrist, Texas</a> – west of High Island.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[95]</a></sup> Estimates of lost homes in the peninsula were around 80%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NGsource_98-0"><a href="#cite_note-NGsource-98">[96]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Southeast Texas communities of Bridge City on Sabine Lake and large areas of nearby <a href="/wiki/Orange,_Texas" title="Orange, Texas">Orange</a> (80 miles or 130 kilometres from the center of landfall) were inundated by the storm surge which traveled as much as 16 miles (26 km) inland from the coast. Bridge City mayor Kirk Roccaforte estimated that only about 14 homes (later updated to around two dozen) in the city were unaffected by the surge.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[97]</a></sup></p>
<p>NASA's <a href="/wiki/Johnson_Space_Center" title="Johnson Space Center">Johnson Space Center</a> suffered minor roof damage to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mission_Control" title="Mission Control">Mission Control</a> and minor cosmetic damage to some of its other buildings. NASA's operations at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ellington_Field" title="Ellington Field">Ellington Field</a> also sustained roof and awning damage,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[98]</a></sup> and one hangar was severely damaged.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Farther_Inland">Farther Inland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Ike&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Farther Inland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ike_2008_rainfall.gif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="901" data-file-width="792" height="250" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Ike_2008_rainfall.gif/220px-Ike_2008_rainfall.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Ike_2008_rainfall.gif/330px-Ike_2008_rainfall.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Ike_2008_rainfall.gif/440px-Ike_2008_rainfall.gif 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ike_2008_rainfall.gif" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Ike's storm total rainfall across the United States</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Effects_of_Hurricane_Ike_in_inland_North_America" title="Effects of Hurricane Ike in inland North America">Effects of Hurricane Ike in inland North America</a></div>
<p>On September 14, after Ike became <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Extratropical_transition" title="Extratropical transition">extratropical</a> and was enhanced by an upper-level <a href="/wiki/Shortwave_(meteorology)" title="Shortwave (meteorology)">shortwave</a> trough, a major wind event took place across the lower and middle Ohio Valley and lower Great Lakes, and significant rainfall and flooding took place to the west. The St. Louis Metropolitan Area experienced hurricane conditions, with Ike's remnants inflicting severe damage to homes. Several areas in <a href="/wiki/Illinois" title="Illinois">Illinois</a> and <a href="/wiki/Indiana" title="Indiana">Indiana</a>, already flooded by the frontal boundary to the north, saw significant additional rainfall.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KCStar_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-KCStar-101">[99]</a></sup> Due to flooding in Chicago, <a href="/wiki/Todd_Stroger" title="Todd Stroger">Todd Stroger</a> declared a state of emergency for <a href="/wiki/Cook_County,_Illinois" title="Cook County, Illinois">Cook County</a> due to flooding of the <a href="/wiki/Des_Plaines_River" title="Des Plaines River">Des Plaines River</a>. Hurricane-force wind gusts were reported to the east of the center across parts of <a href="/wiki/Kentucky" title="Kentucky">Kentucky</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indiana" title="Indiana">Indiana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ohio" title="Ohio">Ohio</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania" title="Pennsylvania">Pennsylvania</a> with significant wind damage including structural damage to buildings and trees. The <a href="/wiki/Louisville,_Kentucky" title="Louisville, Kentucky">Louisville</a> area declared a <a href="/wiki/State_of_emergency" title="State of emergency">state of emergency</a> due to major damage and power outages, and the <a href="/wiki/Louisville_International_Airport" title="Louisville International Airport">Louisville International Airport</a> was closed temporarily. A <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/LG%26E" title="LG&amp;E">LG&amp;E</a> spokesperson said that this was the worst power outage in 30 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Louisville_102-0"><a href="#cite_note-Louisville-102">[100]</a></sup> Later in the day, a statewide state of emergency was declared in Kentucky by <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_Kentucky" title="Governor of Kentucky">Governor</a> <a href="/wiki/Steve_Beshear" title="Steve Beshear">Steve Beshear</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WCPOstate_103-0"><a href="#cite_note-WCPOstate-103">[101]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cincinnati-Northern_Kentucky_International_Airport" title="Cincinnati-Northern Kentucky International Airport">Cincinnati-Northern Kentucky International Airport</a> was also temporarily shut down, and the control tower was evacuated. In <a href="/wiki/Cincinnati" title="Cincinnati">Cincinnati</a>, numerous reports of roof damage and uprooted trees were called in to law enforcement, and on September 15, most of the schools in <a href="/wiki/Hamilton_County,_Ohio" title="Hamilton County, Ohio">Hamilton County</a>, Butler County, and Warren County had classes canceled because of power outages, some of which lasted seven days.</p>
<p>Wind gusts of 75 mph (121 km/h) were recorded in both Cincinnati and <a href="/wiki/Columbus,_Ohio" title="Columbus, Ohio">Columbus</a>, which is equivalent to sustained wind levels found in a Category 1 hurricane.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[102]</a></sup> Additionally, a state of emergency was declared in Ohio.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHIO_105-0"><a href="#cite_note-WHIO-105">[103]</a></sup> Damages in Ohio was originally estimated at $553 million with 131,000 insurance claims filed in the first few days following the storm.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-columbusdi_106-0"><a href="#cite_note-columbusdi-106">[104]</a></sup> The overall total damage in Ohio exceeded $1.1 billion, tying the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1974_Xenia_tornado" title="1974 Xenia tornado">1974 Xenia tornado</a> as the costliest storm in Ohio's history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IkeTCR_3-24"><a href="#cite_note-IkeTCR-3">[2]</a></sup> Also in <a href="/wiki/Salem,_Indiana" title="Salem, Indiana">Salem, Indiana</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Scottsburg,_Indiana" title="Scottsburg, Indiana">Scottsburg, Indiana</a>, wind gusts up to 81 mph (130 km/h) were recorded. In <a href="/wiki/Indiana" title="Indiana">Indiana</a>, high winds caused more than 200,000 customers to be without power throughout the state. Wind gusts of 63 mph (101 km/h) were recorded at <a href="/wiki/Indianapolis_International_Airport" title="Indianapolis International Airport">Indianapolis International Airport</a>.</p>
<p>Coming to <a href="/wiki/Indianapolis" title="Indianapolis">Indianapolis</a>, on September 14, Ike also caused damages to <a href="/wiki/2008_Indianapolis_motorcycle_Grand_Prix" title="2008 Indianapolis motorcycle Grand Prix">the first-ever motorcycle Grand Prix held in Indianapolis</a>, stopping both 125cc and MotoGP races after the two-thirds of the distance, and causing the cancellation of the 250cc race. In <a href="/wiki/Arkansas" title="Arkansas">Arkansas</a>, about 200,000 customers lost power as a result of the winds, the worst power loss in that state since an ice storm in 2000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KARK_107-0"><a href="#cite_note-KARK-107">[105]</a></sup> In the Louisville area, over 300,000 customers were without power — the worst power outage in the utility's history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Louisville_102-1"><a href="#cite_note-Louisville-102">[100]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Cincinnati_metropolitan_area" title="Cincinnati metropolitan area">Cincinnati metropolitan area</a> was hard hit as well, with over 927,000 customers losing power in that region. A <a href="/wiki/Duke_Energy" title="Duke Energy">Duke Energy</a> spokesperson said "We have never seen anything like this. Never. We’re talking about 90 percent of our customers without power." There were so many power outages and so few workers available Duke Energy was thinking of sending workers from their base in <a href="/wiki/Charlotte,_North_Carolina" title="Charlotte, North Carolina">Charlotte, North Carolina</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ohio_deaths_108-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ohio_deaths-108">[106]</a></sup> Many homes and business were without power for 3–7 days. In the Dayton, Ohio area 300,000 of 515,000 Dayton Power &amp; Light Co. customers lost power at some point following severe wind storms on the afternoon of September 14, according to a company spokesperson.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dayton_Daily_News.2C_September_18.2C_2008_109-0"><a href="#cite_note-Dayton_Daily_News.2C_September_18.2C_2008-109">[107]</a></sup> Also hard hit were central Ohio (with over 350,000 customers losing power) and northeastern Ohio (with over 310,000 customers losing power),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GreeleyTrib_110-0"><a href="#cite_note-GreeleyTrib-110">[108]</a></sup> as well as Illinois (49,000),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WTHI_111-0"><a href="#cite_note-WTHI-111">[109]</a></sup> Missouri (85,000),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-STLAmerican_112-0"><a href="#cite_note-STLAmerican-112">[110]</a></sup> and western <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania" title="Pennsylvania">Pennsylvania</a> (with over 180,000 customers losing power).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WTAE_113-0"><a href="#cite_note-WTAE-113">[111]</a></sup> In western Kentucky, outside crews had to be brought in from as far away as <a href="/wiki/Mississippi" title="Mississippi">Mississippi</a> to restore power.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Evansville_114-0"><a href="#cite_note-Evansville-114">[112]</a></sup> In Indiana, about 350,000 customers lost power statewide, mainly in the southern part of the state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Indypower_115-0"><a href="#cite_note-Indypower-115">[113]</a></sup> In New York State, over 100,000 customers were reported without power.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WCAX_116-0"><a href="#cite_note-WCAX-116">[114]</a></sup> In total, 28 deaths have been blamed on Ike in the inland states.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IkeTCR_3-25"><a href="#cite_note-IkeTCR-3">[2]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Canada">Canada</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Ike&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Canada">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Effects_of_Hurricane_Ike_in_inland_North_America" title="Effects of Hurricane Ike in inland North America">Effects of Hurricane Ike in inland North America</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Accumulation_Ike_Canada.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="429" data-file-width="810" height="117" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Accumulation_Ike_Canada.png/220px-Accumulation_Ike_Canada.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Accumulation_Ike_Canada.png/330px-Accumulation_Ike_Canada.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Accumulation_Ike_Canada.png/440px-Accumulation_Ike_Canada.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Accumulation_Ike_Canada.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Accumulations in Canada</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Ontario" title="Ontario">Ontario</a>, Ike's remnants brought a record amount of rain on Sunday, September 14, in the <a href="/wiki/Windsor,_Ontario" title="Windsor, Ontario">Windsor</a> region. It was closely following a slow-moving frontal system that had drenched the city the day before, dumping 75.2 millimeters (2.96 inches) of rain and breaking the old record of 39.1 mm (1.54 in) in 1979, according to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Environment_Canada" title="Environment Canada">Environment Canada</a>. Most damage in the Windsor area with Ike was confined to downed power lines and toppled tree branches with the wind gusts reaching 80 km/h (50 mph), with spotty street flooding that made driving completely treacherous in some areas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WindsorStar_117-0"><a href="#cite_note-WindsorStar-117">[115]</a></sup> Highways were washed out in the <a href="/wiki/Bruce_Peninsula" title="Bruce Peninsula">Bruce Peninsula</a>, and trees were uprooted in <a href="/wiki/London,_Ontario" title="London, Ontario">London, Ontario</a>. The storm continued to cause wind and rain damage as it continues east along the St. Lawrence River leaving around 25,000 customers without electricity, especially in <a href="/wiki/Belleville,_Ontario" title="Belleville, Ontario">Belleville</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brockville,_Ontario" title="Brockville, Ontario">Brockville</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bancroft,_Ontario" title="Bancroft, Ontario">Bancroft</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peterborough,_Ontario" title="Peterborough, Ontario">Peterborough</a>, Bowmanville, <a href="/wiki/Huntsville,_Ontario" title="Huntsville, Ontario">Huntsville</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Timmins,_Ontario" title="Timmins, Ontario">Timmins</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OttawaCityzen_118-0"><a href="#cite_note-OttawaCityzen-118">[116]</a></sup></p>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Quebec" title="Quebec">Quebec</a>, regions to the north of the <a href="/wiki/Saint_Lawrence_River" title="Saint Lawrence River">Saint Lawrence River</a> received 50 mm (2.0 in) to 70 mm (2.8 in) of rainfall (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Laurentides_(region)" title="Laurentides (region)">Hautes-Laurentides</a>, Haute-<a href="/wiki/Mauricie" title="Mauricie">Mauricie</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jacques-Cartier_River" title="Jacques-Cartier River">Réserve faunique des Laurentides</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saguenay-Lac-Saint-Jean" title="Saguenay-Lac-Saint-Jean">Saguenay-Lac-Saint-Jean</a>, <a href="/wiki/Charlevoix" title="Charlevoix">Charlevoix</a> and <a href="/wiki/C%C3%B4te-Nord" title="Côte-Nord">Côte-Nord</a>). Maximum rainfall was recorded between Lac-St-Jean and the Réserve faunique des Laurentides with a station recording more than 90 mm (3.5 in) of rain<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CRIACC_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-CRIACC-119">[117]</a></sup> Along the river, the amount were more in the 10 mm (0.4 in) and 30 mm (1.2 in) range, except in <a href="/wiki/Quebec_City" title="Quebec City">Quebec City</a> area which received almost 50 mm (2.0 in), most of it between 7:00 pm and 8:00 pm.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CRIACC_119-1"><a href="#cite_note-CRIACC-119">[117]</a></sup> This rain caused small inundations, <a href="/wiki/Storm_drain" title="Storm drain">storm drain</a> overflows, and closed one major highway.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SRC_120-0"><a href="#cite_note-SRC-120">[118]</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Montreal" title="Montreal">Montreal</a>, high humidity levels pushed by the system caused electrical malfunction one of the lines of the <a href="/wiki/Montreal_Metro" title="Montreal Metro">subway</a>, stranding over 25,000 commuters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SRC2_121-0"><a href="#cite_note-SRC2-121">[119]</a></sup> High winds up to 78 km/h (48 mph) caused, at their worst, over 25,000 households to lose electricity in <a href="/wiki/Montreal" title="Montreal">Montreal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Laval,_Quebec" title="Laval, Quebec">Laval</a>, <a href="/wiki/Estrie" title="Estrie">Estrie</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mont%C3%A9r%C3%A9gie" title="Montérégie">Montérégie</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SRC3_122-0"><a href="#cite_note-SRC3-122">[120]</a></sup> and when it reached the <a href="/wiki/Magdalen_Islands" title="Magdalen Islands">Magdalen Islands</a>, it had enough strength to cause a sailboat, the <i>Océan</i>, to sink. Its six passengers were rescued by a helicopter of the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Coast_Guard" title="Canadian Coast Guard">Canadian Coast Guard</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CRIACC_119-2"><a href="#cite_note-CRIACC-119">[117]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SRC3_122-1"><a href="#cite_note-SRC3-122">[120]</a></sup></p>
<p>The "Ike Spike" in gasoline prices was quite severe in Canada, with gas prices rising anywhere from 15 to 20 cents per liter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[121]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Iceland">Iceland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Ike&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Iceland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Ike's remnants combined with an unusual depression that affected southwestern <a href="/wiki/Iceland" title="Iceland">Iceland</a> on September 17, three days after Ike became extratropical.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[122]</a></sup> The storm produced 9 m (30 ft) waves along southwest coasts of the island. Rainfall peaked near 200 mm (7.9 in) close to <a href="/wiki/Reykjav%C3%ADk" title="Reykjavík">Reykjavík</a>. Wind gusts were measured up to 89 mph (143 km/h).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[123]</a></sup> Strong winds on the backside of the system produced a large dust storm in northern areas of the island.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[124]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Aftermath">Aftermath</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Ike&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Aftermath">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Turks_and_Caicos_and_the_Bahamas_2">Turks and Caicos and the Bahamas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Ike&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Turks and Caicos and the Bahamas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Due to the damage brought by Ike in the <a href="/wiki/Turks_and_Caicos_Islands" title="Turks and Caicos Islands">Turks and Caicos Islands</a>, the insular government declared the islands of <a href="/wiki/Grand_Turk_Island" title="Grand Turk Island">Grand Turk</a> and <a href="/wiki/South_Caicos" title="South Caicos">South Caicos</a> as <a href="/wiki/Disaster_area" title="Disaster area">disaster areas</a>. Damage on the islands was surveyed immediately following the hurricane's passage by a CDERA assessment team from <a href="/wiki/Jamaica" title="Jamaica">Jamaica</a>. Following the occurrence of extensive power outages, the Caribbean Electric Utilities Services Cooperation offered to support the restoration of power services. The British <a href="/wiki/HMS_Iron_Duke_(F234)" title="HMS Iron Duke (F234)">HMS Iron Duke (F234)</a> was sent to the islands to assist in recovery efforts, and personnel from the British Red Cross were also dispatched.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UpdateCDERASept7TC_127-0"><a href="#cite_note-UpdateCDERASept7TC-127">[125]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Criticism_of_aid">Criticism of aid</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Ike&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Criticism of aid">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>After Hurricane Ike, many residents applied to <a href="/wiki/Federal_Emergency_Management_Agency" title="Federal Emergency Management Agency">FEMA</a> for loans and FEMA trailers. Many residents were forced to wait several weeks until their trailers arrived. Some waited for up to two months, living in hotels, in homes of relatives several miles away, or in their homes, with no power or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Running_water" title="Running water">running water</a>. Many residents were angry at the response that FEMA gave to the problem. Texas state leaders also accused FEMA of foot dragging and insensitivity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[126]</a></sup></p>
<p>$3.1 billion in federal aid was eventually allocated to Texas by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Department_of_Housing_and_Urban_Development" title="Department of Housing and Urban Development">Department of Housing and Urban Development</a>. It was supposed to be used to repair single-family homes of lower and middle-class income families, but as of 2011 only 10% of those funds were released, while the rest were held up because of "state bureaucracy".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aidnyt_129-0"><a href="#cite_note-aidnyt-129">[127]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_and_mental_health_issues">Public and mental health issues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Ike&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Public and mental health issues">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Hurricane Ike also brought many health issues to the victims. Damages from the homes and the environment helped create these issues amongst the public. Following the disaster, communities were challenged to provide the correct medical treatment in emergency rooms and other medical facilities. It developed stress restricting victims their basic health services. Orange County had an 88.5 percent capacity loss of intermediate care facilities reducing its overall capacity. By late October five hospitals that usually served the areas that were impacted by the hurricane stayed closed while only one hospital continued to operate but with a limit of patients.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FEMA_130-0"><a href="#cite_note-FEMA-130">[128]</a></sup></p>
<p>The need for mental health services increased after the disaster especially for depression and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Post-traumatic_stress_disorder" title="Post-traumatic stress disorder">post-traumatic stress disorder</a>. Most individuals will not progress in constant behavioral or mental health problems, but the <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a> estimates between five and ten percent of victims will have more long-term issues.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FEMA_130-1"><a href="#cite_note-FEMA-130">[128]</a></sup> Telephone interviews and mental health diagnoses were ordered randomly to households concerning the effects of Hurricane Ike. Post disaster mental health occurrences were 5.9 percent for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Post-traumatic_stress_disorder" title="Post-traumatic stress disorder">post-traumatic stress disorder</a>, 4.5 percent for <a href="/wiki/Major_depressive_episode" title="Major depressive episode">major depressive episode</a>, and 9.9 percent for general <a href="/wiki/Anxiety_disorder" title="Anxiety disorder">anxiety disorder</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MP_131-0"><a href="#cite_note-MP-131">[129]</a></sup> A Galveston Bay Recovery Study (GBRS) was a survey distributed through a random stratified cluster sampling of victims in the <a href="/wiki/Galveston_Bay" title="Galveston Bay">Galveston Bay</a> area for research on traumatic stress and disaster exposure. When surveyed victims were asked how they felt and what they experienced after the hurricane there was an immediate emotional response of fear from the loss of property, employment, displacement, and damages.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-APA_132-0"><a href="#cite_note-APA-132">[130]</a></sup> Children were targeted for physical abuse by parents and guardians because of loss of property and employment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FEMA_130-2"><a href="#cite_note-FEMA-130">[128]</a></sup> Results of post-traumatic stress disorder, depressive symptoms, anxiety symptoms, dysfunctions, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Disabilities" title="Disabilities">disabilities</a> were reported when asked how stressful their lives have been since Hurricane Ike.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-APA_132-1"><a href="#cite_note-APA-132">[130]</a></sup> There was an increase of impairments, interference with social activities and health behaviors such as eating poorly, smoking more, and restlessness.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-APA_132-2"><a href="#cite_note-APA-132">[130]</a></sup> Development of these mental health problems was due to the lack of sufficient clean clothing, electricity, food, money, transportation, or water for at least one week.</p>
<p>Victims and workers face numerous residential and occupational hazards during the process of repairing their homes or community. An exposure to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hazardous_materials" title="Hazardous materials">hazardous materials</a> through the process created health threats of diseases, air contamination, smoke inhalation, and lead poisoning. As disaster victims return to their damaged homes children were exposed to the <a href="/wiki/Debris" title="Debris">debris</a> and other hazards, developing a risk of injury.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FEMA_130-3"><a href="#cite_note-FEMA-130">[128]</a></sup> After the hurricane because of power outages individuals and family misused portable generators causing <a href="/wiki/Carbon_monoxide_poisoning" title="Carbon monoxide poisoning">carbon monoxide poisoning</a>. Eighty-two percent to 87 percent of carbon monoxide were caused by the improper use of generators. The <a href="/wiki/Texas_Department_of_State_Health_Services" title="Texas Department of State Health Services">Texas Department of State Health Services</a> issued that gasoline generators should not be used indoor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CDC_133-0"><a href="#cite_note-CDC-133">[131]</a></sup> Fifty-four people were reported by the Texas poison centers to have storm related carbon monoxide exposure. The <a href="/wiki/Undersea_and_Hyperbaric_Medical_Society" title="Undersea and Hyperbaric Medical Society">Undersea and Hyperbaric Medical Society</a> and The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Center_for_Disease_Control" title="Center for Disease Control">Center for Disease Control</a> reported 15 people had to undergo hyperbaric oxygen treatment for carbon monoxide poisoning.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CDC_133-1"><a href="#cite_note-CDC-133">[131]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Smith2009_134-0"><a href="#cite_note-Smith2009-134">[132]</a></sup> Symptoms from exposure were headaches, nausea, and vomiting with the majority of the treated cases under the age of eighteen.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Smith2009_134-1"><a href="#cite_note-Smith2009-134">[132]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[133]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Ike&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Hurricane Ike forced the <a href="/wiki/Houston_Astros" title="Houston Astros">Houston Astros</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Cubs" title="Chicago Cubs">Chicago Cubs</a> to play out their 3-game set in <a href="/wiki/Milwaukee" title="Milwaukee">Milwaukee</a> at <a href="/wiki/Miller_Park_(Milwaukee)" title="Miller Park (Milwaukee)">Miller Park</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[134]</a></sup> Ike also forced the postponement of the second-week NFL game between the Houston Texans and the Baltimore Ravens. The game was later made up in Houston after repairs were made to Reliant Stadium on November 9, 2008. It also forced the NCAA football game on September 13 between the <a href="/wiki/Houston_Cougars_football" title="Houston Cougars football">Houston Cougars</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Air_Force_Falcons_football" title="Air Force Falcons football">Air Force Falcons</a> to be moved from <a href="/wiki/Robertson_Stadium" title="Robertson Stadium">Robertson Stadium</a> in Houston to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gerald_Ford_Stadium" title="Gerald Ford Stadium">Gerald Ford Stadium</a> in Dallas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[135]</a></sup> Ike also forced the postponement of a Texas Longhorns game in Austin,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[136]</a></sup> Texas due to increased evacuee traffic in the city's shelters. Tickets for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World_Wrestling_Entertainment" title="World Wrestling Entertainment">World Wrestling Entertainment</a> (WWE) <a href="/wiki/WrestleMania_XXV" title="WrestleMania XXV">WrestleMania XXV</a> were originally scheduled to go on sale September 20, 2008, but it was postponed due to the effect of Ike on the state of Texas until November 8, 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ticketsalespost_139-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ticketsalespost-139">[137]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[138]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Relief_efforts">Relief efforts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Ike&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Relief efforts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>There were a number of relief efforts set up to help those caught up in Ike, including one set up by <a href="/wiki/Portlight_Strategies" title="Portlight Strategies">Portlight</a> and <a href="/wiki/Weather_Underground_(weather_service)" title="Weather Underground (weather service)">Weather Underground</a>. Most of them raised at least $10,000 to help out.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[139]</a></sup> The Portlight/Weather Underground effort created some initial controversy springing from the unexpected overwhelming response to requests for assistance.</p>
<p>Portlight delivered over $500,000 worth of equipment to people with disabilities and outlying communities that were impacted by Hurricane Ike. They also delivered pizza to the residents of the hard-hit Bolivar peninsula and helped provide a Christmas party for residents of Bridge City, Texas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[140]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[141]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Oil_and_gas_spills">Oil and gas spills</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Ike&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Oil and gas spills">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Hurricane Ike's winds, surge, and giant waves tossed storage tanks and punctured pipelines. However, operators in the Gulf of Mexico (ranging from major integrated producers like BP and Shell to small privately owned independents) shut in operations in advance of Ike's approach as a precautionary measure. As a result of these shut-ins, US oil production dropped from 5 million barrels per day (790,000 cubic meters per day) to 4 Mbbl/d (640,000 m<sup>3</sup>/d) in the immediate aftermath of the hurricane. By late November, production was restored to pre-Ike levels. Despite the hurricane, only 500,000 U.S. gallons (1,900 cubic meters) of crude oil spilled into the Gulf of Mexico and the marshes, bayous and bays of Louisiana and Texas over a coastline distance of 185 miles (298 kilometres). Much of the spillage occurred in the High Island area of Galveston County, Texas, where storm surge rose over a low-lying oilfield and flooded the marshy area around several producing wells, beam pumps and storage tanks. During the days both before and after the storm, companies, and residents reported around 448 releases of gas, oil and other substances into the environment in Louisiana and Texas. The hardest hit places were industrial centers near Houston and Port Arthur, Texas, as well as oil production facilities off Louisiana's coast.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DOFmain_144-0"><a href="#cite_note-DOFmain-144">[142]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coast_Guard" title="Coast Guard">Coast Guard</a>, with the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Environmental_Protection_Agency" title="United States Environmental Protection Agency">Environmental Protection Agency</a> and state agencies, has responded to more than 3,000 pollution reports associated with the storm and its surge along the upper Texas coast. Most callers complain about abandoned <a href="/wiki/Propane" title="Propane">propane</a> tanks, paint cans and other hazardous materials containers turning up in marshes, backyards, and other places.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[143]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Oil_Tanker_SKS_Satilla_collision_against_a_missing_oil_rig">Oil Tanker SKS <i>Satilla</i> collision against a missing oil rig</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Ike&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Oil Tanker SKS Satilla collision against a missing oil rig">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On March 6, 2009, a 159,000-ton Norwegian tanker <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=SKS_Satilla&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="SKS Satilla (page does not exist)">SKS <i>Satilla</i></a> collided with a jackup oil rig <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ensco_International" title="Ensco International">Ensco 74</a>, which had been missing after Ike struck.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[144]</a></sup> The tanker's double hull prevented an oil spill at the site 65 miles south of Galveston, which is 115 miles west of the original position of the rig.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[145]</a></sup> Four drilling rigs including Ensco 74 were damaged by Ike, but it was the only rig missing. At least fifty-two oil platforms were damaged by Ike.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[146]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Retirement">Retirement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Ike&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Retirement">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_retired_Atlantic_hurricane_names" title="List of retired Atlantic hurricane names">List of retired Atlantic hurricane names</a></div>
<p>Because of the tremendous damage, number of deaths, and people left missing, the name <b>Ike</b> was officially retired on April 22, 2009 by the <a href="/wiki/World_Meteorological_Organization" title="World Meteorological Organization">World Meteorological Organization</a>, and will never be used again for an <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_hurricane" title="Atlantic hurricane">Atlantic tropical cyclone</a>. It was replaced with <i>Isaias</i> in the 2014 season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[147]</a></sup> <i>Isaias</i>, however, was not used in 2014, so it could be used in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2020_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2020 Atlantic hurricane season">2020</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[148]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Future_mitigation">Future mitigation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Ike&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Future mitigation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Ike_Dike" title="Ike Dike">Ike Dike</a></div>
<p>A commission was established by <a href="/wiki/Rick_Perry" title="Rick Perry">Rick Perry</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_Texas" title="Governor of Texas">Texas Governor</a>, following the hurricane to investigate preparing for and mitigating future disasters. A proposal has been put forth to build an "<a href="/wiki/Ike_Dike" title="Ike Dike">Ike Dike</a>", a massive <a href="/wiki/Levee" title="Levee">levee</a> system which would protect the <a href="/wiki/Galveston_Bay" title="Galveston Bay">Galveston Bay</a>, and the important industrial facilities which line the coast and the <a href="/wiki/Houston_Ship_Channel" title="Houston Ship Channel">ship channel</a>, from a future, potentially more destructive storm. The proposal has gained widespread support from a variety of business interests. As of 2009<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Ike&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, it is currently only at the conceptual stage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151">[149]</a></sup></p>
